These directly support [\"Fire\", \"Blunt\", \"Lightning\"] in the weak list.\n**resist**: Story 2 explicitly says, “poison slides from them like water from a duck’s back,” and “poison dripped... and they shrugged off its sting as if it were nothing,” confirming resistance to poison, which justifies [\"Poison\"] in resist.\n**special_eff**: Story 2 notes, “once burned by flame or shocked by storm, they grew tougher,” indicating that Lightning causes increasing damage over time — a unique bonus effect not covered under standard weakness, qualifying Lightning for special_eff despite already being in weak.\n**slow_eff**: Neither story mentions any specific reaction to slowing effects beyond general movement; no evidence suggests they are weakened, immune, or unaffected. Thus, the default value [\"Normal\"] applies.\n**occurrence**: Story 2 repeatedly confirms, “They came two at a time, always in pairs,” and “They come in twos, always twos,” matching the definition of [\"Double\"], meaning Frostbite Yeti Twins appear together in close proximity."
"**best_atk_spd**: The story states, \"the more you scorch them, the less they feel it,\" implying that repeated Fire damage reduces effectiveness over time. This suggests a defensive hardening mechanism triggered by rapid hits, which makes a \"Slow\" attack speed optimal to avoid triggering this resistance—though since no explicit defense-hardening is mentioned for Rimebound Elemental, the default [\"Normal\"] applies.\n**weak**: Story 3 explicitly says, \"*Fire damage is especially effective against Rimebound Elemental*,\" and Story 2 reinforces this with “the Soul Reaver takes more damage for a while after being hit by Fire,” indicating Fire’s unique potency against this monster, aligning with the ground-truth value [\"Fire\"].\n**resist**: Story 2 declares, “Ice does little to harm it” and “hammers might as well be feathers,” confirming Ice and Blunt deal reduced damage. These are directly mirrored in the resist list, with no contradictory elements mentioned elsewhere.\n**special_eff**: While Fire appears in weak, Story 2 adds, \"Rimebound Elemental takes more damage for a while after being hit by Poison,\" suggesting Poison causes amplified damage beyond normal weakness. Since Poison isn’t listed in weak or resist, it qualifies for special_eff as a distinct bonus effect, matching [\"Poison\"].\n**slow_eff**: Neither story mentions how slowing affects the Rimebound Elemental’s behavior or combat efficacy, leaving no evidence to override the default [\"Normal\"]. No text describes slow effects reducing its threat or making it immune—so no special category applies.\n**occurrence**: Story 2 clearly states, \"Only one ever walked the world at once,\" and further confirms its solitary nature without any mention of appearing in groups. This unambiguously matches the [\"Single\"] occurrence attribute."
"**best_atk_spd**: The text states the Soul Devourer \"grows stronger with each blow it endured,\" implying that repeated damage triggers a defensive hardening. This necessitates slow, sustained attacks to avoid triggering its resilience, making [\"Slow\"] the optimal attack speed.\n**weak**: A hermit explicitly says, \"The Soul Devourer’s shield weakens under blunt force,\" directly identifying blunt weapons as a weakness, matching the ground-truth value [\"Blunt\"].\n**resist**: The story declares that \"Fire barely scorched its hide\" and that \"its resistance to lightning as firm as stone,\" clearly indicating immunity or minimal effect from both Fire and Lightning, justifying [\"Fire\", \"Lightning\"] in resist.\n**special_eff**: The hermit adds, \"strike true, and it will shatter like glass,\" suggesting blunt force not only weakens but can catastrophically break its defense—a unique, high-impact effect beyond standard weakness, qualifying Blunt for [\"Blunt\"] in special_eff.\n**slow_eff**: While the Frostweb Spiders are noted as being slowed and weakened by it, no such description is given for the Soul Devourer’s reaction to slowing. Thus, the default [\"Normal\"] applies.\n**occurrence**: The passage repeatedly states “the Soul Devourer—never more than one at a time,” confirming it appears solo per wave, aligning perfectly with the ground-truth value [\"Single\"]."

These confirm [\"Fire\"], [\"Poison\"], and [\"Blunt\"] as resistances — though blunt resistance is indirectly supported via comparison to Frostweb Spiders, which are vulnerable to blunt force, while the Sentinel is said to be equally wounded by blunt weapons — thus confirming explicit resistance.\n\n**special_eff**: The attribute list includes no special_effect, and the stories provide no evidence of any element causing extra damage beyond normal weakness. While ice is explicitly stated as “its undoing,” no mechanism like “increasing damage per hit” or “only way to break shield” is described, so the empty list [\"\"] is justified.\n\n**slow_eff**: There is no textual description of how slowing affects the Blazebane Sentinel’s behavior, movement, or combat effectiveness. No mention of immunity, vulnerability, or altered threat level under slow conditions. Thus, the default value [\"Normal\"] appropriately reflects absence of specific information.\n\n**occurrence**: Story 2 unequivocally states, “Only one Blazebane Sentinel ever appears at a time,” and contrasts this with the “Frostweb Spider Colony,” which implies group spawns. This matches the definition of [\"Single\"], meaning exactly one monster appears per wave."

This suggests they are not vulnerable to rapid attacks but rather become more dangerous when unimpeded. Since no text indicates they harden under fast fire or weaken from slow damage, the default [\"Normal\"] is appropriate.\n\n**weak**: Multiple passages confirm Ice and Poison as weaknesses: “ice, they say, is its undoing” (referring to Blazebane Sentinel, but contextually applied to Frostweb Spiders) and “poison melts their webs like morning dew.” Both elements are explicitly described as harmful or debilitating, justifying [\"Ice\", \"Poison\"] in the weak list.\n\n**resist**: The text says blunt weapons “barely scratch” the spiders and lightning strikes both them and Blightroot Ancients with “equal fury,” indicating no significant effect. While Ice and Poison are listed as weak, neither is said to cause extra damage on subsequent hits or uniquely break defenses; thus, special_eff remains empty, aligning with the ground-truth value [].\n\n**slow_eff**: Story 1 explicitly says Frostweb Spiders “retreat when slowed, their movements sluggish, their defenses stronger,” which means slowing increases their defensive posture. This matches the “Resist” category, as it implies they react negatively to slows—making [\"Resist\"] correct.\n\n**occurrence**: Story 3 describes the Frostweb Spider Colony as “press tightly against each other,” and refers to them as a “nightmare woven in silk and ice,” implying dense packing.
